# Garage Audit — Jarvis / ISAC / Alice Codebase
**Generated:** 2025 (manual audit pass)
**Scope:** All files provided in the current chat context
**Purpose:** Reference document — what each file does, what it connects to, and its value to the Alice project.

---

## How to Read This Document

Each entry covers:
- **What it does** — the file's primary job
- **Connects to** — direct imports, dependencies, or callers
- **Alice value** — what this file is worth to the Alice project specifically

---

## Infrastructure & Deployment

---

### `docker-compose.yml`

**What it does:**
Defines the three-service Docker stack: `jarvis-agent` (nginx static file server), `jarvis-brain` (FastAPI Python backend), and `jarvis-runner` (execution sidecar). Wires environment variables, port bindings, volume mounts, and a shared Docker network (`jarvis_net`).

**Connects to:**
- `jarvis-brain` → `/opt/jarvis/brain` (build context), `/opt/jarvis/brain-data` (data volume), `/opt/jarvis` (project root mount)
- `jarvis-runner` → `/opt/jarvis` (project root mount)
- `jarvis-agent` → `/opt/jarvis/data` (static HTML)
- All services share `jarvis_net`

**Alice value:**
High. This is the deployment contract. Alice's brain runs inside `jarvis-brain`. The runner sidecar is Alice's execution arm for filesystem and shell operations. The agent serves the UI Alice talks through. Any change to Alice's runtime environment starts here.

---

## Brain — Core Application

---

### `brain/main.py`

**What it does:**
The central FastAPI application. This is the largest and most complex file in the project. It:
- Initializes the LLM client, HA client, Grocy client, BarcodeBuddy client
- Defines all API routes directly or via included routers
- Implements the Alice Gate (Bundle 1 context integrity, Bundle 5 ethics/oversight)
- Implements the Task Ledger (create, list, get, abort, resume)
- Implements the Execution Spine (resume logic for file write, diff apply, ingestion gates, MAP/PACK/PROMOTE postures, governed observation, tool calls)
- Implements the Fix-It protocol (`/fixit/*`)
- Implements the Alice unified turn endpoint (`/alice/turn`)
- Implements Chat Working State (CWS v1) — session-only rolling transcript
- Implements Doc Learning v1 — read-only extract + confirm flow
- Implements Working Memory v2 — disk-backed YAML memory tree
- Implements the finance router (read-only snapshot)
- Implements the calendar router (read-only HA calendar)
- Implements the Grocy router (stock, shopping list, products, locations, barcode inspect/create)
- Implements the BarcodeBuddy router
- Implements the Home Assistant router
- Implements the runner proxy router
- Implements admin unlock (PIN → short-lived token)
- Implements sandbox boundary enforcement
- Implements lineage, timing, and failure tracking hooks (referenced but defined elsewhere)

**Connects to:**
- `model_client.py` — LLM calls
- `services/homeassistant.py` — HA client
- `services/grocy.py` — Grocy client
- `services/barcodebuddy.py` — BarcodeBuddy client
- `services/openfoodfacts.py` — OFF barcode lookup
- `services/identity_manager.py` — admin role check
- `services/recipes.py`, `ingredient_parser.py`, `recipe_matcher.py`, `recipe_analyzer.py`, `recipe_mappings.py`, `mealplans.py`, `mealplanner.py` — sub-routers
- `alice_preview_router.py` — Alice Phase 8 preview
- `alice_gate.py` — advance gate logic
- `alice/memory_api.py` — Alice memory router
- `alice/name_resolution.py` — alias resolution
- `health_capture.py`, `system_health_capture.py` — health snapshots
- `services/irr_ups.py`, `services/irr_narrative.py` — IRR routers
- `services/finance_reader.py` — finance snapshot reader
- `tools/task_ledger.py` — task CRUD
- `tools/executor.py` — tool execution
- `tools/registry.py` — tool allowlist
- `tools/types.py` — ToolRequest/ToolResult
- `tools/okd/artifacts.py` — OKD plan storage
- `tools/okd/governed_observation.py` — governed observation execution
- `identity_memory/db.py` — DB connect/schema
- `continuity.py` — conversation history
- `identity_memory/router.py` — identity/memory v1 routers

**Alice value:**
Critical. This is Alice's brain stem. Every capability Alice has — conversation, tool use, memory, task execution, governance gates, Fix-It, doc learning — is either implemented here or routed through here. Understanding this file is understanding Alice.

---

### `brain/model_client.py`

**What it does:**
Defines the abstract `ModelClient` interface and two concrete implementations:
- `OpenAICompatibleClient` — calls any OpenAI-compatible `/v1/chat/completions` endpoint
- `GeminiModelClient` — placeholder (not implemented, raises on use)

Also provides `build_model_client_from_env()` factory and `_normalize_api_base()` to prevent double `/v1` paths.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` (`MODEL_CLIENT.generate_chat_completion(...)`)
- Used by Fix-It, Alice turn, doc learning, and any other model call site in `main.py`

**Alice value:**
High. Alice's intelligence runs through this interface. Swapping providers, adding streaming, or adding structured output support all happen here. The abstraction is clean and correct.

---

## Brain — Alice Subsystems

---

### `brain/alice_gate.py`

**What it does:**
Implements the behavioral advance gate (`advance_gate()`). Determines whether a user message should result in `ADVANCE_OK`, `RESTRAIN`, `PAUSE`, or similar decisions. Also exports `GateDecision` enum and `is_continuation_phrase()`.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` inside `alice_gate_advance()` (the `/alice/gate/advance` endpoint)
- Imports from `alice/types.py` (IsacSignal, AliceMove, etc.)

**Alice value:**
High. This is Alice's behavioral governor. Every message passes through this gate before Alice acts. Bundle 1 (context integrity) and Bundle 5 (ethics/oversight) wrap around it in `main.py`.

---

### `brain/alice/types.py`

**What it does:**
Defines the core Alice type system:
- `IsacSignalKind` — enum of signal types
- `BoundaryType` — enum of boundary categories
- `AliceMove` — enum of Alice's possible moves
- `ConfidenceLevel` — enum
- `Confidence` — frozen dataclass
- `BoundaryNotice` — frozen dataclass
- `IsacSignal` — frozen dataclass (the primary signal object)

**Connects to:**
- Used by `alice_gate.py`
- Used by `alice/_selftest.py`

**Alice value:**
High. These types are the vocabulary of Alice's governance layer. Any new signal type, boundary, or move must be added here first.

---

### `brain/alice/language.py`

**What it does:**
Provides `normalize_whitespace(s)` — a simple utility to collapse runs of whitespace in a string.

**Connects to:**
- Likely used by gate logic or signal processing in `alice_gate.py` or related modules

**Alice value:**
Low individually, but part of the Alice language normalization pipeline. Correct whitespace handling prevents false gate decisions.

---

### `brain/alice/name_resolution.py`

**What it does:**
Implements alias-to-concept resolution for Alice. Given a text string and a user ID, looks up whether the text matches a known user-specific alias in the SQLite DB (`memory_aliases` table). Returns a concept dict if matched.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` in the `/ask` endpoint (Phase 8 name resolution)
- Uses `identity_memory/db.py` for DB connection
- Reads from `memory_aliases` and `memory_concepts` tables

**Alice value:**
High. This is how Alice learns that "the pantry" means a specific Grocy location, or that "Kaitlyn's account" means a specific finance account. It's the bridge between human language and structured system concepts.

---

### `brain/alice/memory_api.py`

**What it does:**
FastAPI router for the Alice memory API (`/alice/memory/*`). Provides:
- `GET /alice/memory/health`
- `GET /alice/memory/concepts`
- `GET /alice/memory/aliases`
- `GET /alice/memory/aliases/by-concept/{concept_id}`
- `GET /alice/memory/aliases/by-user/{user_id}`
- `POST /alice/memory/concepts` (admin)
- `POST /alice/memory/aliases` (admin)
- `DELETE /alice/memory/concepts/{concept_id}` (admin)

Currently gated by `_lap_memory_inactive_guard()` — all endpoints return 403 during the Last Administrative Phase (LAP). Also enforces sandbox boundary.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `alice_memory_router`
- Reads/writes `memory_concepts` and `memory_aliases` SQLite tables
- Uses `identity_memory/db.py` for DB path

**Alice value:**
High (future). Currently inactive (LAP guard). When activated, this is how Alice's concept and alias memory is managed via API. The schema-safe insert logic (`_insert_schema_safe`) is well-designed and worth preserving.

---

### `brain/alice/_selftest.py`

**What it does:**
A standalone self-test script for Alice signal types. Prints formatted signal cases for manual inspection. Not part of the running application.

**Connects to:**
- Uses `alice/types.py` (IsacSignal, etc.)

**Alice value:**
Low for production, useful for development. Helps verify that signal types are correctly constructed before wiring them into the gate.

---

## Brain — Services

---

### `brain/services/homeassistant.py`

**What it does:**
Home Assistant HTTP API client. Provides both sync (`requests`) and async (`asyncio.to_thread`) methods for:
- Health check
- Get config
- List/get states
- List services
- Call service

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (`HA_CLIENT`)
- Used by `system_health_capture.py`
- Used by calendar router in `main.py`

**Alice value:**
High. Home Assistant is Alice's window into the physical home — lights, switches, sensors, automations. This client is Alice's hands and eyes in the house.

---

### `brain/services/grocy.py`

**What it does:**
Grocy HTTP API client supporting multiple household instances (`home_a`, `home_b`). Provides:
- Health check
- Stock overview
- Shopping list
- Products, locations, quantity units
- Create product, create location, link barcode, add stock

Uses `httpx` for async HTTP. Supports household routing via `_select_instances()`.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (Grocy router, barcode router, confirm-create endpoint)
- Configured via `GROCY_HOME_A_*` and `GROCY_HOME_B_*` env vars

**Alice value:**
High. Grocy is Alice's food/household inventory system. Barcode scanning, meal planning, shopping lists, and stock management all flow through this client.

---

### `brain/services/barcodebuddy.py`

**What it does:**
Async HTTP client for Barcode Buddy (scan-only). Provides:
- `health()` — check BB status
- `scan_barcode(barcode)` — submit a barcode scan

Intentionally scan-only. No product creation, no shopping list writes via BB directly.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (barcode router)
- Configured via `BARCODEBUDDY_BASE_URL` and `BARCODEBUDDY_API_KEY`

**Alice value:**
Medium. Barcode Buddy is the physical scan entry point. When someone scans a barcode in the kitchen, it flows through here. The scan-only constraint is correct and intentional.

---

### `brain/services/openfoodfacts.py`

**What it does:**
Read-only OpenFoodFacts client for barcode lookup. Provides:
- `lookup_barcode(barcode)` — GET `/api/v2/product/{barcode}.json`
- `extract_suggestion_from_off_payload(payload)` — extract name/brand/category from OFF response

Gate A compliant: no writes, pure lookup.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` in `grocy_inspect_barcode()` as external fallback when barcode not found in Grocy

**Alice value:**
Medium. Fills the gap when a barcode is unknown to Grocy. Provides a starting suggestion for product creation without requiring manual entry.

---

### `brain/services/finance_reader.py`

**What it does:**
Read-only finance snapshot reader. Reads a local JSON snapshot file (Firefly III export) and provides:
- `read_finance_snapshot()` — raw JSON
- `summarize_finances()` — account balances + inflow/outflow totals
- `list_transactions(days, limit, offset)` — windowed, paged transaction listing

No live API calls. No writes.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (finance router: `/finance/summary`, `/finance/transactions`, `/finance/health`)
- Reads from `FINANCE_SNAPSHOT_PATH` (default `/app/data/finance/snapshots/latest.json`)

**Alice value:**
Medium. Gives Alice read-only visibility into household finances. The snapshot model is correct — no live bank connections, no writes. Useful for budget awareness and spending summaries.

---

### `brain/services/finance_manager.py`

**What it does:**
A stub/scaffold class `FinanceManager` with placeholder methods for:
- `ingest_snapshot()` — ingest transactions into memory
- `classify_transaction()` — categorize a transaction
- `detect_anomalies()` — find spending outliers
- `calculate_velocity()` — spending rate
- `summarize_spending()` — by category/period
- `forecast_spending()` — predict future spend
- `run_budget_check()` — compare against budget
- `find_transactions()` — natural language search
- `get_account_balance()` — read account balance

All methods are stubs with `print()` statements and placeholder return values. Not wired into any router.

**Connects to:**
- Nothing currently (not imported anywhere in the provided files)
- Designed to work with a `memory_api` object

**Alice value:**
Low currently (all stubs), but the interface design is valuable. This is the right shape for Alice's future finance intelligence layer. Worth keeping as a design document and filling in when the memory API is activated.

---

### `brain/services/identity_manager.py`

**What it does:**
Loads a `users.yaml` file and provides:
- `get_user_role(username)` — returns role string or None
- `is_admin(username)` — returns bool

Used to gate admin-only operations in `main.py`.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` in `alice_set_execution_posture()` to verify admin role
- Reads from `brain-data/memory/users.yaml`

**Alice value:**
Medium. Simple but necessary. Provides the human identity layer that determines who can do what. The YAML-backed approach is fragile for production but acceptable for a homelab. Worth migrating to the SQLite users table eventually.

---

### `brain/services/irr_ups.py`

**What it does:**
Read-only IRR (Infrastructure Reliability & Resilience) router for UPS monitoring. Provides:
- `GET /irr/ups/latest` — latest UPS poll line + snapshot file
- `GET /irr/ups/log` — tail or since-filtered UPS log

Reads from `/irr/ups_poll.log` and `/irr/ups_snapshot_*.txt`. No writes, no commands.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `irr_router`
- Reads from `/irr/` mount directory

**Alice value:**
Medium. UPS awareness is important for a homelab. Alice knowing the UPS status, battery percentage, and runtime allows her to warn about power events and avoid scheduling heavy tasks during low-battery periods.

---

### `brain/services/ingredient_parser.py`

**What it does:**
Parses natural language ingredient lines (e.g., "2 cups flour, sifted") into structured `ParsedIngredient` objects with quantity, unit, name, and preparation fields. Provides a FastAPI router.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `ingredient_parser_router`

**Alice value:**
High for meal planning. Alice needs to parse recipe ingredients to match them against Grocy stock, generate shopping lists, and scale recipes. This is a core NLP utility for the food domain.

---

### `brain/services/recipe_analyzer.py`

**What it does:**
Provides recipe analysis logic and a FastAPI router. Normalizes ingredient strings for comparison.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `recipe_analyzer_router`

**Alice value:**
Medium-High. Part of the recipe intelligence pipeline. Analyzing recipes for nutritional content, ingredient availability, or substitution suggestions is a natural Alice capability.

---

### `brain/services/recipe_mappings.py`

**What it does:**
Manages mappings between recipe ingredient names and Grocy product names. Provides CRUD endpoints for mappings stored in SQLite. Supports household-scoped mappings.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `recipe_mappings_router`
- Uses SQLite for persistence

**Alice value:**
High. The gap between "recipe says flour" and "Grocy has King Arthur All-Purpose Flour" is bridged here. Without this, Alice can't reliably match recipes to inventory.

---

### `brain/services/recipe_matcher.py`

**What it does:**
Matches recipe ingredients against Grocy inventory. Provides `MatchCandidate`, `IngredientMatchResult`, and `GrocyMatchIngredientsResponse` models, plus a FastAPI router.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `recipe_matcher_router`

**Alice value:**
High. This is how Alice answers "can I make this recipe tonight?" — by checking what's in stock against what the recipe needs.

---

### `brain/services/recipes.py`

**What it does:**
Full recipe management system. Handles:
- Recipe drafts (create, update, finalize)
- Finalized recipe snapshots
- Grocy integration for recipe ingredients
- Schema migration for recipe tables
- Ingredient parsing and scaling

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `recipes_router`
- Uses SQLite for recipe storage
- Integrates with Grocy for ingredient matching

**Alice value:**
High. Recipes are a central use case. Alice helping plan meals, generate shopping lists from recipes, and track what's been cooked requires a solid recipe store.

---

### `brain/services/mealplans.py`

**What it does:**
Meal plan management. Handles meal plan items, shopping preview generation, and scaling recipes for meal plans. Provides a FastAPI router.

**Connects to:**
- Mounted in `main.py` as `mealplans_router` (under `/mealplans`)
- Uses SQLite
- Reads from finalized recipe snapshots

**Alice value:**
High. Meal planning is one of Alice's most practical household capabilities. This is the persistence layer for "what are we eating this week."

---

## Brain — Tools

---

### `brain/tools/registry.py`

**What it does:**
Defines the tool registry — the authoritative list of all tools Alice can use. Each tool has a name, family (`WEB`, `UTILITY`, `LOCAL_READ`), and description. Provides:
- `TOOL_DEFS` — dict of all tools
- `V4A_ENABLED_TOOLS` — current phase allowlist
- `is_known_tool()` — existence check
- `is_tool_allowed()` — allowlist gate

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (tool call endpoints, `/tools/call`, task resume)
- Used by `tools/executor.py`
- Used by `tools/okd/governed_observation.py`

**Alice value:**
Critical. This is the tool allowlist. Adding a new tool to Alice requires adding it here first. The family-based gating (WEB/UTILITY/LOCAL_READ) is the right abstraction for phase-controlled capability expansion.

---

### `brain/tools/executor.py`

**What it does:**
Single canonical tool execution entry point (`run_tool()`). Routes tool requests to the correct family handler:
- `web` → `run_web_tool()`
- `utility` → `run_utility_tool()`
- `local_read` → `run_local_read_tool()`

Enforces sandbox boundary (if `governance_ctx={"sandbox": True}`). Enforces tool allowlist. Fills in timing fields on results.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` (task resume, `/tools/call`, alice turn tool calls)
- Calls `tools/web_tools.py`, `tools/utility_tools.py`, `tools/local_read_tools.py`
- Uses `tools/registry.py` for allowlist checks
- Uses `tools/types.py` for request/result types

**Alice value:**
Critical. Every tool Alice uses goes through this function. It's the execution choke point — the right place to add governance checks, rate limiting, or observability hooks.

---

### `brain/tools/types.py`

**What it does:**
Defines the tool type system:
- `ToolFailureClass` — enum of failure categories (TOOL_NOT_ALLOWED, TOOL_INTERNAL_ERROR, SANDBOX_BOUNDARY, etc.)
- `ToolProvenance` — dataclass with source URL, fetched_at, etc.
- `ToolRequest` — dataclass with tool_name, args, purpose, task_id, step_id, user_id, chat_id
- `ToolResult` — dataclass with ok, tool_name, failure_class, primary, provenance, timing

**Connects to:**
- Used by `tools/executor.py`, `tools/web_tools.py`, `tools/utility_tools.py`, `tools/local_read_tools.py`
- Used by `main.py` for tool call endpoints

**Alice value:**
High. Clean, typed interfaces for tool I/O. The `ToolFailureClass` enum is particularly valuable — it enables structured failure handling rather than string matching on error messages.

---

### `brain/tools/task_ledger.py`

**What it does:**
SQLite-backed task ledger. Provides:
- `create_task(title, resume_hint)` — create a pending task
- `add_step(task_id, step_index, description)` — add a step
- `add_artifact(task_id, artifact_type, path, metadata_json, step_id)` — store an artifact
- `create_tool_call_task(tool_name, args, purpose)` — convenience wrapper

**Connects to:**
- Used extensively by `main.py` for all task creation and artifact storage
- Uses SQLite (same DB as identity/memory)

**Alice value:**
Critical. The task ledger is Alice's audit trail and execution spine. Every action Alice takes — file writes, tool calls, ingestion runs — is recorded here. Without this, there's no accountability, no resume-on-failure, and no human visibility into what Alice did.

---

### `brain/tools/local_read_tools.py`

**What it does:**
Implements local filesystem read tools:
- `local.read_file` — read a file (allowlisted paths)
- `local.read_snippet` — read a line range from a file
- `local.list_dir` — list directory contents
- `local.tree` — render a bounded directory tree
- `local.grep` — search text for a pattern

All are read-only. Path allowlisting enforced.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `tools/executor.py`
- Uses `tools/types.py`

**Alice value:**
High. These tools give Alice the ability to read her own codebase, config files, and data directories. Essential for self-awareness, doc learning, and debugging.

---

### `brain/tools/utility_tools.py`

**What it does:**
Implements utility tools:
- `util.time` — get current time for a timezone offset
- `util.weather` — get weather forecast
- `util.calc` — evaluate a safe arithmetic expression (AST-based, no eval)

**Connects to:**
- Called by `tools/executor.py`
- Uses `tools/types.py`

**Alice value:**
Medium. Time and weather are frequently needed for household planning. The safe calculator is useful for recipe scaling and budget math.

---

### `brain/tools/web_tools.py`

**What it does:**
Implements web retrieval tools:
- `web.search` — search the web
- `web.open` — open a URL
- `web.find` — find text in an opened page
- `web.click` — follow a link
- `web.screenshot_pdf` — screenshot a PDF page
- `web.read_site` — bounded same-domain crawl

**Connects to:**
- Called by `tools/executor.py`
- Uses `tools/types.py`

**Alice value:**
High. Web search and reading are Alice's primary research tools. Doc learning, the learn intent in alice/turn, and any research task depend on these.

---

### `brain/tools/okd/artifacts.py`

**What it does:**
Stores and retrieves OKD (Operational Knowledge Domain) artifacts in the task ledger:
- `store_plan()` / `okd_store_plan()` — store an observation plan
- `store_plan_approval()` / `okd_store_plan_approval()` — record admin approval
- `load_latest_plan()` / `okd_load_latest_plan()` — retrieve latest plan
- `is_plan_approved()` / `okd_is_plan_approved()` — check approval status
- `append_expansion_event()` — log observation events
- `store_expansion_log()`, `store_update_brief()` — store OKD outputs

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` (governed observation endpoints, task resume)
- Uses `tools/task_ledger.py` for artifact storage

**Alice value:**
High. OKD governed observation is Alice's structured research protocol — the mechanism by which Alice can safely explore the web under an approved plan. The plan/approval/execute pattern is the right governance model.

---

### `brain/tools/okd/governed_observation.py`

**What it does:**
Executes a governed observation under an approved plan. Orchestrates tool calls (web search, open, find) within the scope of the approved observation plan. Produces expansion log and update brief artifacts.

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` in task resume (governed_observation title)
- Uses `tools/executor.py` for tool calls
- Uses `tools/okd/artifacts.py` for artifact storage
- Uses `tools/registry.py` for tool allowlist

**Alice value:**
High. This is Alice's structured research execution engine. It's the difference between Alice randomly browsing the web and Alice conducting a bounded, auditable, admin-approved research session.

---

## Brain — Supporting Modules

---

### `brain/continuity.py`

**What it does:**
Provides `get_history(conn, session_id, limit)` — retrieves conversation history from SQLite for a given chat session. Used by the `/history` endpoint.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` in the `/history` endpoint
- Uses the shared SQLite DB connection

**Alice value:**
Medium. Conversation continuity is important for Alice to maintain context across messages. This is the persistence layer for that continuity.

---

### `brain/health_capture.py`

**What it does:**
Captures internal health metrics (`capture_internal_health()`) — returns a `HealthAggregate` with validation snapshots for internal services.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` in `/health/isac_internal`
- Uses `validators/health.py` and `validators/base.py`

**Alice value:**
Medium. Internal health visibility helps Alice (and admins) know when something is degraded before it causes a user-facing failure.

---

### `brain/system_health_capture.py`

**What it does:**
Captures external/system health (`capture_system_health(ha_client)`) — checks Home Assistant connectivity and other external dependencies. Returns a structured health dict.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `main.py` in `/health/system`
- Uses `services/homeassistant.py`

**Alice value:**
Medium. Knowing that HA is reachable (or not) before attempting to control lights or read sensors prevents confusing failures.

---

### `brain/validators/base.py`

**What it does:**
Defines the `ValidatorStatus` enum and `BaseValidator` Protocol — the interface all validators must implement.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `validators/health.py`
- Used by `health_capture.py`

**Alice value:**
Low individually. Part of the validation framework. The Protocol-based interface is clean and extensible.

---

### `brain/validators/health.py`

**What it does:**
Defines `HealthAggregate` — an in-memory container for validation snapshots. Provides `add()`, `get_domain()`, and `domains()` methods. Passive container: no decisions, no persistence, no scoring.

**Connects to:**
- Used by `health_capture.py`
- Used by `main.py` (health endpoints)

**Alice value:**
Low individually. Part of the health observability stack. The "passive container" design is correct — health aggregation should not make decisions.

---

## Governance & Canonical Documents

---

### `governance/canonical/project_spine.md`

**What it does:**
The canonical project identity document. Defines what Alice is, what she is not, how she operates, and the non-negotiable invariants. Explicitly states that this document overrides all others in case of conflict.

Key statements:
- Alice is "life infrastructure" and a "life co-processor"
- Alice is expected to act, learn, and improve
- Avoiding action out of fear is failure
- Non-negotiable invariants: honesty, explicit uncertainty, auditability, visible recovery, learning from failure, no silent irreversible actions, preservation of human trust

**Connects to:**
- Referenced conceptually by all Alice behavior
- Should be loaded into Alice's context for any governance decision

**Alice value:**
Critical. This is the north star. When Alice is uncertain about whether to act or wait, this document answers the question. When a developer is uncertain about whether a new feature fits the project, this document answers the question. It should be treated as load-bearing.

---

## Database Schema

---

### `identity_memory_v1.sql`

**What it does:**
SQLite migration script for the Identity & Memory v1 schema. Creates:
- `users` — user registry with lifecycle status (provisional/reinforced/permanent)
- `user_lifecycle_events` — audit log of user state changes
- `memory_items` — key-value memory per user with tier, confidence, and expiry
- `memory_events` — audit log of memory changes
- `admin_inbox` — pending admin notifications

Additive-only, idempotent (uses `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`).

**Connects to:**
- Applied to the SQLite DB at `JARVIS_DB_PATH`
- Schema used by `identity_memory/db.py` and the identity/memory v1 routers

**Alice value:**
High. This is the schema for Alice's user model and memory system. The lifecycle status model (provisional → reinforced → permanent) is the right approach for a system that needs to earn trust before storing durable facts.

---

## Runner

---

### `runner/main.py`

**What it does:**
The runner sidecar FastAPI application. Provides:
- `GET /runner/health` — health check
- File content, web fetch, and tree endpoints (based on the summary)
- Execution primitives that the brain proxies through

**Connects to:**
- Called by `main.py` (brain) via `_runner_get()` and the runner router
- Runs as a separate container (`jarvis-runner`)

**Alice value:**
High. The runner is Alice's execution arm. File reads, directory listings, and eventually shell commands go through here. The separation between brain (reasoning) and runner (execution) is architecturally correct and important for safety.

---

## Verification

---

### `verify_phases.py`

**What it does:**
A verification script that calls the brain API to check that phase-gated features are working correctly. Uses `get_admin_token()`, `call()`, and `run()` to exercise endpoints.

**Connects to:**
- Calls the brain API externally
- Uses admin token auth

**Alice value:**
Medium. Automated verification is important for a system that self-modifies. This script is the seed of a proper test suite. Worth expanding significantly.

---

## Key Observations

### What's Working Well
1. **Governance layering** — Bundle 1 (context integrity), Bundle 5 (ethics/oversight), and the advance gate form a coherent behavioral governance stack.
2. **Task ledger + execution spine** — The pending → resume → complete pattern with artifacts is the right model for auditable, recoverable execution.
3. **Tool allowlist** — The registry + executor pattern cleanly separates "what tools exist" from "what tools are allowed right now."
4. **Household scoping** — The home_a/home_b pattern throughout Grocy, calendar, and stock is consistent and correct.
5. **Read-only defaults** — Finance, calendar, and barcode inspection are all read-only by default. Writes require explicit confirmation.

### What Needs Attention
1. **`finance_manager.py`** — All stubs. Needs implementation when memory API is activated.
2. **`alice/memory_api.py`** — LAP-gated (all 403). Needs activation plan.
3. **`identity_manager.py`** — YAML-backed, fragile. Should migrate to SQLite users table.
4. **`verify_phases.py`** — Thin. Needs expansion into a proper test suite.
5. **`alice/_selftest.py`** — Manual only. Should be automated.

### Architectural Gaps
1. No background job scheduler — Alice can't proactively check things without a user message.
2. No push notification path — Alice can't alert the user without being asked.
3. Memory activation — The memory system exists in schema and API but is LAP-gated. The activation plan needs to be defined.
4. Finance execution — Globally blocked. The unblocking path and authority model need to be defined before this can be enabled.

---
